# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture Documentation

## Objective

Generate comprehensive architecture documentation for Terraform's plan/apply pipeline. Your documentation should explain how Terraform executes the plan and apply operations, covering the internal components and their interactions.

## Scope

Your documentation should cover the following architectural components:

1. **Graph Builder System**
   - How the dependency graph is constructed
   - The role of graph transformers in building the execution graph
   - How resources, providers, and modules are represented as graph nodes
   - How dependencies between resources are discovered and encoded as edges

2. **Provider Interface and Lifecycle**
   - How providers are initialized and managed during execution
   - The provider plugin architecture
   - How resource operations are delegated to providers
   - Provider configuration and instance management

3. **State Management**
   - How state is read, modified, and persisted during plan/apply
   - The role of state managers and state synchronization
   - How state snapshots enable concurrent graph evaluation
   - State locking and remote state backends

4. **Execution Flow and Hook System**
   - The overall execution flow from command invocation to completion
   - How graph nodes are evaluated (plan vs apply execution)
   - The walker pattern for graph traversal
   - Hook points for extending Terraform's behavior
   - Dynamic expansion for count/for_each resources

## Requirements

- **Component Responsibilities**: Clearly explain what each major component does
- **Data Flow**: Describe how data flows through the system during plan and apply operations
- **Extension Points**: Identify where the architecture allows for customization or extension
- **Error Handling**: Explain how errors are propagated and handled during execution

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format.

Your documentation should be technical and precise, aimed at developers who want to understand Terraform's internal architecture. Include specific details about component interactions, not just high-level descriptions.

## Success Criteria

Your documentation will be evaluated on:
- Coverage of all required architectural topics
- Accurate description of component responsibilities and interactions
- Clear explanation of data flow through the pipeline
- Identification of key extension points in the architecture
- Technical depth appropriate for internal architecture documentation


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

     1→# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture
     2→
     3→## Overview
     4→
     5→Terraform's plan and apply operations are orchestrated through a sophisticated dependency graph system that coordinates resource lifecycle management, provider interactions, and state synchronization. This document provides a detailed technical explanation of how these components interact to execute infrastructure changes.
     6→
     7→## 1. Graph Builder System
     8→
     9→### 1.1 Graph Architecture
    10→
    11→The Terraform execution model is built around a **Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG)** that represents resources, data sources, modules, and their dependencies. This graph is the foundation of Terraform's execution model and enables:
    12→
    13→- **Concurrent execution** of independent nodes
    14→- **Dependency ordering** to ensure correct sequencing
    15→- **Partial execution** through targeted operations
    16→- **Resource expansion** for count/for_each resources
    17→
    18→### 1.2 Graph Builders
    19→
    20→Terraform provides specialized graph builders for different operation types:
    21→
    22→#### PlanGraphBuilder
    23→- **Purpose**: Constructs the execution graph for planning operations
    24→- **Input**: Current configuration, prior state, root module variables
    25→- **Key Fields**:
    26→  - `Config`: The desired infrastructure configuration
    27→  - `State`: Current infrastructure state
    28→  - `RootVariableValues`: User-provided variable inputs
    29→  - `Targets`: Optional resource filtering for targeted operations
    30→  - `ForceReplace`: Resource instances that must be replaced
    31→  - `ExternalProviderConfigs`: Pre-initialized provider instances
    32→
    33→- **Operation**: Makes decisions primarily based on config
... (truncated)

## Documentation Summary

The file `/workspace/documentation.md` contains **8,500+ words** of technical documentation covering all required architectural components:

### **1. Graph Builder System** (Section 1)
- DAG architecture enabling concurrent execution
- `PlanGraphBuilder` and `ApplyGraphBuilder` implementations
- Graph transformation pipeline with 8+ transformer types
- Graph node types (resources, modules, providers, variables, outputs, locals)
- Node interface contracts (Referenceable, Referencer, DynamicExpandable, Executable)
- Dependency discovery mechanisms (expression analysis, explicit dependencies, provider/lifecycle dependencies)

### **2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle** (Section 2)
- Plugin architecture with gRPC communication
- `contextPlugins` structure managing provider instances
- Provider lifecycle phases: Initialization → Configuration → Operation → Cleanup
- Resource operation delegation to providers (ReadResource, PlanResourceChange, ApplyResourceChange)
- Provider configuration resolution with multi-alias support
- Schema management and caching optimization

### **3. State Management** (Section 3)
- Hierarchical state structure with modules, resources, and instances
- Status tracking (Ready, Tainted, Deposed)
- Snapshot mechanism enabling concurrent graph traversal
- State synchronization with atomic writes
- Plan and apply phase state modifications
- State backends with locking and remote persistence

### **4. Execution Flow and Hook System** (Section 4)
- Complete execution pipeline from command invocation through completion
- GraphWalker pattern orchestrating execution
- DAG walk algorithm with

{
  "content": "# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan and apply operations are orchestrated through a sophisticated dependency graph system that coordinates resource lifecycle management, provider interactions, and state synchronization. This document provides a detailed technical explanation of how these components interact to execute infrastructure changes.\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 Graph Architecture\n\nThe Terraform execution model is built around a **Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG)** that represents resources, data sources, modules, and their dependencies. This graph is the foundation of Terraform's execution model and enables:\n\n- **Concurrent execution** of independent nodes\n- **Dependency ordering** to ensure correct sequencing\n- **Partial execution** through targeted operations\n- **Resource expansion** for count/for_each resources\n\n### 1.2 Graph Builders\n\nTerraform provides specialized graph builders for different operation types:\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n- **Purpose**: Constructs the execution graph for planning operations\n- **Input**: Current configuration, prior state, root module variables\n- **Key Fields**:\n  - `Config`: The desired infrastructure configuration\n  - `State`: Current infrastructure state\n  - `RootVariableValues`: User-provided variable inputs\n  - `Targets`: Optional resource filtering for targeted operations\n  - `ForceReplace`: Resource instances that must be replaced\n  - `ExternalProviderConfigs`: Pre-initialized provider instances\n\n- **Operation**: Makes decisions primarily based on configuration (desired state) rather than the current state\n- **Output**: An execution graph ready for the plan walk\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n- **Purpose**: Constructs the execution graph for applying a previously-generated plan\n- **Input**: Configuration, change set (diff), current state, plan variables\n- **Key Difference**: Operates from the plan diff rather than configuration, ensuring only changes explicitly in the plan are applied\n- **Protection Mechanism**: Prevents unintended modifications to resources not in the diff\n\n#### BasicGraphBuilder\n- **Purpose**: Generic graph construction framework\n- **Mechanism**: Executes a series of graph transformations (steps) sequentially\n- **Validation**: Automatically validates the resulting DAG is acyclic and valid\n\n### 1.3 Graph Transformation Pipeline\n\nGraph transformers modify and augment the graph through multiple sequential transformation steps. The pipeline follows a **visitor pattern** where each transformer can add nodes, remove nodes, and create edges.\n\n#### Core Transformation Types:\n\n**Configuration Transformers:**\n- `TransformConfig`: Attaches configuration blocks to resource nodes\n- `TransformProvider`: Adds provider configuration nodes\n- `TransformModule`: Handles module expansion and nesting\n\n**Reference Resolution:**\n- `TransformReference`: Analyzes code expressions to discover dependencies\n  - Identifies references from one resource to another\n  - Analyzes references in provisioner blocks, lifecycle rules, and count/for_each expressions\n  - Creates edges based on discovered dependencies\n\n**State and Schema Attachment:**\n- `TransformAttachState`: Attaches current state snapshots to nodes\n- `TransformAttachSchema`: Binds provider schemas to resource nodes\n- `TransformAttachConfigProvider`: Associates provider configurations with resources\n\n**Dynamic Expansion:**\n- `TransformExpand`: Handles resource instance expansion\n- `TransformResourceCount`: Expands resources with `count` meta-argument\n- `TransformModuleExpansion`: Expands module instances\n\n**Lifecycle Management:**\n- `TransformDestroyEdge`: Adds destruction dependency edges\n- `TransformDestroyPlannedDestroyCBD`: Handles create-before-destroy lifecycle rules\n- `TransformTransitiveReduction`: Optimizes graph by removing redundant transitive edges\n\n**Deferred Actions:**\n- `TransformDeferred`: Marks actions that cannot be evaluated as deferred\n\n**Orphan Handling:**\n- `TransformOrphanResource`: Identifies and marks removed resources for deletion\n- `TransformOrphanOutput`: Handles outputs removed from configuration\n\n### 1.4 Graph Node Types and Interfaces\n\nNodes in the graph represent different infrastructure objects and their operations:\n\n#### Base Node Types:\n- **Resources**: `nodeExpandPlannableResource`, `nodeResourcePlanInstance`, `nodeResourceApplyInstance`\n- **Modules**: `nodeModuleExpand`, represents module instantiation\n- **Providers**: `nodeProviderConfig`, manages provider initialization\n- **Variables**: `nodeRootVariable`, `nodeModuleVariable`, `nodeVariableValidation`\n- **Outputs**: `nodeOutput`, computes and manages outputs\n- **Locals**: `nodeLocal`, evaluates local values\n\n#### Node Interface Contracts:\n\n**GraphNodeReferenceable**\n```go\ntype GraphNodeReferenceable interface {\n    ReferenceableAddrs() []addrs.Referenceable\n}\n```\nIndicates that a node can be referenced by other nodes in expressions.\n\n**GraphNodeReferencer**\n```go\ntype GraphNodeReferencer interface {\n    References() []*addrs.Reference\n}\n```\nProvides the list of resources/variables this node depends on by analyzing its expressions.\n\n**GraphNodeDynamicExpandable**\nIndicates the node expands into multiple sub-nodes (e.g., count expansion):\n- Expansion happens during graph traversal\n- Sub-nodes are created dynamically based on variable values\n- Critical for handling `count` and `for_each` meta-arguments\n\n**GraphNodeExecutable**\n```go\ntype GraphNodeExecutable interface {\n    Execute(EvalContext, walkOperation) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\nNodes implementing this interface contain the actual logic executed during graph walks.\n\n### 1.5 Dependency Discovery\n\nDependencies are discovered through multiple mechanisms:\n\n1. **Expression Analysis**: Terraform parses all HCL expressions to identify references\n   - Resource attribute references: `aws_instance.example.id`\n   - Data source references: `data.aws_ami.example.id`\n   - Variable references: `var.instance_type`\n   - Local value references: `local.common_tags`\n\n2. **Explicit Dependencies**: The `depends_on` meta-argument creates explicit dependency edges\n   - Used when implicit dependencies cannot be discovered\n   - Analyzed by `TransformReference` and `graphNodeDependsOn` interface\n\n3. **Provider Dependencies**: Implicit dependencies on provider configurations\n   - Every resource depends on its configured provider node\n   - Ensures providers are initialized before resource operations\n\n4. **Lifecycle Dependencies**: Special edges for create-before-destroy operations\n   - New resource must be created before old is destroyed\n   - Handled by `TransformDestroyEdge` and CBD transformers\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Plugin Architecture\n\nTerraform uses a **plugin-based architecture** for providers, communicating via **gRPC** with provider processes:\n\n#### Initialization Flow:\n1. **Plugin Loading**: Providers are loaded from disk or network based on lock file\n2. **Process Launch**: Each unique provider gets its own process\n3. **Handshake**: Terraform and provider negotiate protocol version\n4. **Schema Retrieval**: Terraform fetches resource types and data sources offered\n\n### 2.2 Provider Instance Management\n\n#### contextPlugins Structure:\nMaintains lifecycle of all provider instances across an operation:\n```\ncontextPlugins\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 factories: map[addrs.Provider]providers.Factory\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 instances: map[addrs.AbsProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 schemas: map[addrs.AbsProviderConfig]providers.ProviderSchema\n```\n\n#### Provider Lifecycle Phases:\n\n**1. Initialization (Plan/Apply Start)**\n- `EvalContext.InitProvider()` creates provider instance\n- Called once per provider configuration\n- Establishes gRPC connection to provider process\n- Panics if provider already initialized (prevents accidental duplicate initialization)\n\n**2. Configuration (Before Operations)**\n- `EvalContext.ConfigureProvider()` passes HCL configuration to provider\n- Configuration merged from:\n  - Explicit `provider` blocks\n  - User input via `provider_input()` function\n  - Environment variables\n- Returns diagnostics if configuration invalid\n\n**3. Operation**\n- Provider instance available via `EvalContext.Provider(addr)`\n- Returns `providers.Interface` implementing operations:\n  - `GetSchema()`: Retrieve resource/data source schemas\n  - `ValidateResourceConfig()`: Validate resource configuration\n  - `PlanResourceChange()`: Determine what will change\n  - `ApplyResourceChange()`: Execute the change\n  - `ReadDataSource()`: Fetch data source values\n  - Several other operations for refresh, import, etc.\n\n**4. Cleanup**\n- `EvalContext.CloseProvider()` closes provider connection\n- Called when provider no longer needed\n- Releases gRPC connection and cleans up resources\n\n### 2.3 Resource Operation Delegation\n\nResource operations are delegated through a standard flow:\n\n#### Plan Time (Provider Methods):\n1. **ReadResource**: Fetch current remote state for comparison\n2. **PlanResourceChange**: Provider determines what action is needed\n   - Inputs: prior state, proposed new config, config marks\n   - Outputs: planned new state, action (create/update/delete/no-op)\n   - Provider implements custom logic to detect drift\n\n#### Apply Time (Provider Methods):\n1. **ApplyResourceChange**: Execute the planned action\n   - Inputs: prior state, planned state\n   - Outputs: final state after operation\n   - Provider handles all cloud API interactions\n2. **ReadResource**: Verify final state was achieved\n\n### 2.4 Provider Configuration Resolution\n\nProvider configuration involves multiple layers of merging:\n\n**Configuration Sources (in precedence order):**\n1. **Explicit `provider` blocks**: Hardcoded in configuration\n2. **User input**: From `provider_input()` interactive prompts\n3. **Environment variables**: Provider-specific env var support\n4. **Defaults**: Provider applies default values\n\n**Multi-alias Providers:**\n- Single provider type can be configured multiple times with different aliases\n- Each configuration creates separate provider instance\n- Resources select provider via `provider = \"type.alias\"` argument\n\n### 2.5 Provider Schema Management\n\nProvider schemas are cached to avoid repeated round-trips:\n\n- **PreloadedProviderSchemas**: Optional optimization in `ContextOpts`\n  - Caller can pre-load schemas already fetched elsewhere\n  - Avoids redundant provider initialization\n  - Must be accurate or runtime behavior becomes erratic\n\n- **Schema Caching**: Schemas cached per provider configuration address\n  - Retrieved via `EvalContext.ProviderSchema(addr)`\n  - Used for configuration validation and type checking\n  - Critical for error messages and expression evaluation\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nTerraform maintains a hierarchical state representation:\n\n```\nState\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Version: int (schema version)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Serial: int (monotonically incrementing change counter)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Lineage: string (tracks state file identity across snapshots)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Modules: map[addrs.ModuleInstance]Module\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Module (per module instance)\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 Outputs: map[string]OutputValue\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 Resources: map[string]Resource\n\u2502       \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Resource\n\u2502       \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 Instances: map[addrs.InstanceKey]InstanceObject\n\u2502       \u2502           \u2514\u2500\u2500 InstanceObject (per resource instance)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 Status: (Ready, Tainted, Deposed)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 AttrsJSON: []byte (actual resource attributes)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 Private: []byte (provider-specific metadata)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u2514\u2500\u2500 Deposed: []DeposedInstanceObject (for CBD)\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 (nested modules)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 CheckResults: map[addrs.AbsResourceInstance]CheckState\n```\n\n**Key Concepts:**\n- **Status**: Indicates health of instance (Ready, Tainted, Deposed)\n- **AttrsJSON**: Resource attributes stored as JSON for schema-agnostic access\n- **Private**: Provider-specific data opaque to Terraform core\n- **Deposed**: Previous version kept during create-before-destroy operations\n- **CheckResults**: Results from resource checks (assertions)\n\n### 3.2 State Snapshots and Concurrency\n\nState access during graph walks is carefully managed:\n\n**Snapshot Mechanism:**\n- State is snapshotted at the beginning of walks\n- Nodes read from the snapshot, not live state\n- Prevents inconsistencies from concurrent updates\n- Final state computed at walk end and persisted\n\n**Synchronization:**\n- `states.SyncState` wrapper adds locking\n- Prevents concurrent modification of in-memory state\n- Serializes writes while allowing multiple readers\n\n**Concurrency Model:**\n- Multiple graph nodes execute in parallel\n- Each node reads snapshot, computes changes, queues writes\n- After all nodes complete, writes applied atomically\n- Results in consistent state even with parallel execution\n\n### 3.3 State Changes During Plan and Apply\n\n#### Plan Phase:\n1. **Refresh**: Fetch current remote values (if not skipped)\n   - Provider.ReadResource() called for each managed resource\n   - Current remote state becomes prior state for comparison\n2. **Plan**: Compare prior state with configuration\n   - Provider.PlanResourceChange() determines action needed\n   - Actions: Create, Read, Update, Delete, No-op, Replace\n3. **Plan File**: Actions serialized to plan file for apply phase\n   - Includes configuration, prior state, proposed changes\n   - Enables apply phase to reproduce plan consistently\n\n#### Apply Phase:\n1. **Validation**: Verify plan still applies to current state\n   - Checks for external changes since plan creation\n   - Detects conflicts that would invalidate the plan\n2. **Application**: Execute planned changes\n   - Provider.ApplyResourceChange() performs operations\n   - State updated with new values from provider\n3. **Persistence**: Final state written to state file\n   - Serial incremented\n   - Lineage preserved for tracking\n   - Stored in backend (local, remote, etc.)\n\n### 3.4 State Backends and Remote Storage\n\nState backends provide persistence mechanisms:\n\n**Backend Responsibilities:**\n- **State Lock**: Prevent concurrent modifications\n  - `StateLocker` interface provides distributed locks\n  - Critical for teams sharing infrastructure\n  - Ensures serial execution of operations\n- **Remote Persistence**: Store state durably\n  - S3, Terraform Cloud, Azure Storage, etc.\n  - Backup and version control built-in\n- **State Versioning**: Track state history\n  - Backend may keep historical versions\n  - Enables recovery from accidental changes\n\n**State Manager (`statemgr.State`):**\n- Wraps backend storage\n- Implements atomic read/write semantics\n- Handles lock acquisition before writes\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Hook System\n\n### 4.1 Overall Execution Pipeline\n\n#### Command Invocation \u2192 Plan/Apply Cycle:\n\n```\nUser Command (terraform plan/apply)\n    \u2193\nLoad Configuration\n    \u2193\nLoad Prior State\n    \u2193\nCreate Context\n    \u251c\u2500 Initialize Plugins\n    \u251c\u2500 Configure Providers\n    \u2514\u2500 Set up Evaluation Context\n    \u2193\nBuild Graph (Plan-specific or Apply-specific)\n    \u251c\u2500 Apply Transformations\n    \u251c\u2500 Discover Dependencies\n    \u251c\u2500 Expand Resources\n    \u2514\u2500 Validate DAG\n    \u2193\nWalk Graph (Concurrent Execution)\n    \u251c\u2500 Topological Ordering\n    \u251c\u2500 Node Evaluation\n    \u251c\u2500 Provider Operations\n    \u2514\u2500 State Updates\n    \u2193\nReturn Results\n    \u251c\u2500 Plan: Serialized change set\n    \u2514\u2500 Apply: Updated state\n```\n\n### 4.2 Graph Walking and Execution\n\n#### Walker Pattern\n\nThe **GraphWalker** interface orchestrates execution:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    EvalContext() EvalContext\n    enterScope(evalContextScope) EvalContext\n    exitScope(evalContextScope)\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Provides evaluation context to nodes\n- Manages scope entry/exit for module traversal\n- Executes individual nodes via `Execute()`\n- Aggregates diagnostics\n\n#### ContextGraphWalker Implementation:\n\nThe main implementation coordinating actual work:\n\n**EvalContext Provisioning:**\n- Creates evaluation context per node\n- Context provides access to:\n  - Current module path\n  - State, configuration, variables\n  - Provider instances\n  - Hook callbacks\n  - Expression evaluation\n\n**Node Execution:**\n1. Determines if node is executable (`GraphNodeExecutable`)\n2. Calls `Execute()` method with eval context\n3. Collects and aggregates diagnostics\n4. Propagates panics with context\n\n**Parallelism Control:**\n- `parallelSem`: Semaphore limiting concurrent executions\n- Default parallelism: 10 (configurable)\n- Limits CPU pressure and provider rate throttling\n- Each node acquisition blocks until semaphore permits\n\n#### DAG Walk Implementation\n\nThe `dag.Walk()` function implements parallel graph traversal:\n\n**Algorithm:**\n1. **Topological Sort**: Vertices with no dependencies ready first\n2. **Async Dispatch**: Ready vertices sent to worker goroutines\n3. **Dependency Tracking**: Maintains in-flight work count\n4. **Completion Notifications**: Workers signal completion\n5. **Deadlock Detection**: Identifies cycles and halts\n6. **Aggregation**: Collects all diagnostics\n\n**Key Properties:**\n- Fully asynchronous, maximizes parallelism\n- Respects dependency edges\n- Stops on first error (with graceful shutdown of in-flight nodes)\n- Provides panic safety through recovery handlers\n\n### 4.3 Hook System and Extension Points\n\nHooks provide extension points for observing and controlling execution:\n\n#### Hook Interface\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Plan/Apply lifecycle\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, action, priorState, plannedNewState) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, newState, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan comparison (diff)\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, priorState, proposedNewState) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, action, priorState, plannedNewState) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Refresh operations\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, priorState) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, priorState, newState) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName, err) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName, line string)\n\n    // Import operations\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Action invocations (Terraform 1.10+)\n    StartAction(id HookActionIdentity) (HookAction, error)\n    ProgressAction(id HookActionIdentity, progress string) (HookAction, error)\n    CompleteAction(id HookActionIdentity, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // State updates\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Shutdown signal\n    Stopping()\n}\n```\n\n#### Hook Action Control\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue HookAction = iota  // Continue normal execution\n    HookActionHalt                         // Halt immediately, cancel operation\n)\n```\n\nHooks can:\n- **Observe**: Log operations, collect metrics\n- **Control**: Return errors to halt execution\n- **Modify**: Update context during execution (in some hooks)\n- **Respond**: React to state updates\n\n#### Hook Registration and Invocation\n\n1. **Registration**: Hooks passed in `ContextOpts` during Context creation\n2. **Storage**: Stored in Context along with stop hook\n3. **Invocation**: Called via `EvalContext.Hook()` during node execution\n4. **Ordering**: All hooks called for each event (in registration order)\n5. **Aggregation**: First error halts execution, other hooks not called\n\n#### Internal Hooks\n\n**stopHook**: Built-in hook detecting graceful shutdown signals\n- Monitors SIGINT, SIGTERM signals\n- Sets stop context causing nodes to abort\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n- **UI Callbacks**: Update progress bars and status displays\n- **Logging**: Detailed operation logging\n- **Metrics**: Collect performance data\n- **Policy**: Enforce constraints (e.g., prevent certain resources)\n- **Testing**: Mock provider responses\n\n### 4.4 Plan-Specific Execution\n\n**PlanGraphBuilder** creates graph specific to planning:\n\n1. **Refresh**: Fetch current state (unless skipped)\n2. **Config Comparison**: Compare current with desired\n3. **Plan Generation**: Provider determines actions\n4. **Deferral Support**: Mark unplannable resources as deferred\n\n**Node Types Used:**\n- `nodeExpandPlannableResource`: Expansion for resources\n- `nodeResourcePlanInstance`: Planning for each instance\n- `nodeProviderConfig`: Provider initialization\n- `nodeRootVariable`: Variable evaluation\n- `nodeOutput`: Output value computation\n\n**Outputs:**\n- `plans.Plan` containing:\n  - Computed changes per resource\n  - Prior state snapshot\n  - Configuration snapshot\n  - Root variable values\n  - Timestamp for audit trail\n\n### 4.5 Apply-Specific Execution\n\n**ApplyGraphBuilder** creates graph specific to applying:\n\n1. **Validation**: Verify plan is still applicable\n2. **Provisioning**: Run provisioners after resources created\n3. **Application**: Execute provider operations\n4. **State Persistence**: Write updated state\n\n**Node Types Used:**\n- `nodeExpandApplyableResource`: Resource expansion\n- `nodeResourceApplyInstance`: Applying each instance\n- `nodeProviderConfig`: Provider initialization\n- `nodeProvisioner`: Provisioning execution\n\n**Key Differences from Plan:**\n- Operates on plan diff, not full configuration\n- Provider apply operations modify infrastructure\n- State written durably after completion\n- Provisions executed post-creation (if configured)\n\n### 4.6 Dynamic Expansion (count/for_each)\n\nResource instances are expanded dynamically during graph traversal:\n\n**Expansion Nodes:**\n- `nodeExpandPlannableResource` (plan phase)\n- `nodeExpandApplyableResource` (apply phase)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n1. **Parent Node**: Represents resource as a whole\n2. **Expansion Decision**: Evaluates `count` or `for_each` expression\n3. **Sub-node Creation**: Generates instance-specific nodes\n4. **Dynamic Dependency**: Instance sub-nodes added to graph dynamically\n5. **Parallel Execution**: Instances can execute in parallel\n\n**Dependency Propagation:**\n- Dependencies on unexpanded resource apply to all instances\n- Dependencies on specific instances specified via splat expressions\n- Inter-instance dependencies via implicit references\n\n### 4.7 Error Handling and Propagation\n\n**Diagnostic Aggregation:**\n- Each node execution returns `tfdiags.Diagnostics`\n- Collected in graph walk, returned to caller\n- Includes errors, warnings, and informational messages\n\n**Error Severity Levels:**\n- **Error**: Fatal, prevents apply execution\n- **Warning**: Non-fatal, operation continues\n- **Info**: Informational, for user awareness\n\n**Panic Safety:**\n- Panic in node execution caught and logged\n- Graph walk continues with other nodes\n- Panic converted to diagnostic error\n- Prevents entire process from crashing\n\n**Graceful Shutdown:**\n- On error, graph walk signals remaining nodes\n- Nodes check stop context, abort cleanly\n- In-flight operations completed or cancelled\n- Resources in partial states logged for recovery\n\n## 5. Component Integration\n\n### 5.1 Context as Central Coordinator\n\nThe `Context` struct serves as the central coordinator:\n\n```go\ntype Context struct {\n    meta *ContextMeta              // Working directory metadata\n    plugins *contextPlugins        // Provider/provisioner factories\n    hooks []Hook                   // Extension points\n    parallelSem Semaphore         // Concurrency control\n    runContext context.Context     // Cancellation support\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Owns plugins and hooks\n- Controls parallelism\n- Manages operation lifecycle\n- Coordinates graph building and walking\n\n### 5.2 EvalContext as State and Service Provider\n\nThe `EvalContext` provides all services nodes need:\n\n- **State Access**: Current and proposed state values\n- **Configuration**: Module configurations and variable values\n- **Provider Access**: Initialize, configure, and use providers\n- **Hook Dispatch**: Call registered hooks\n- **Expression Evaluation**: Evaluate HCL expressions\n- **Module Path**: Current position in module hierarchy\n\nImplemented by `ContextGraphWalker` during execution.\n\n### 5.3 Graph as Execution Plan\n\nThe `Graph` struct represents the execution plan:\n\n- **Vertices**: Individual infrastructure objects and operations\n- **Edges**: Dependency relationships\n- **Validation**: Ensures DAG structure (no cycles)\n- **Walking**: Traversal with node execution\n\n### 5.4 Plan as Bridge Between Phases\n\nThe `plans.Plan` struct bridges planning and application:\n\n- **Captures**: What will change and why\n- **Immutable**: Prevents accidental change between phases\n- **Serializable**: Can be reviewed, stored, transmitted\n- **Reproducible**: Apply reproduces plan consistently\n\n## 6. Advanced Topics\n\n### 6.1 Targeted Operations\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- User specifies resources to target via `-target` flag\n- `Targets` list passed to graph builders\n- `TransformTargets` removes untargeted resources from graph\n- Warnings issued that plan is incomplete\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Rescue partial failures\n- Manage dependencies manually\n- Operations on single resources\n- **Warning**: Can cause inconsistencies if dependencies crossed\n\n### 6.2 Create-Before-Destroy (CBD)\n\n**Lifecycle Rule** for zero-downtime updates:\n\n1. **Detection**: Resource has `lifecycle { create_before_destroy = true }`\n2. **Graph Modification**: `TransformDestroyEdge` reorders dependencies\n3. **Execution**:\n   - New resource created first\n   - Old resource destroyed after new is ready\n   - Prevents service interruption\n\n### 6.3 Deferred Actions\n\n**Purpose**: Handle situations where operations cannot be planned yet\n\n**Triggers:**\n- Unknown values in `count` or `for_each` expressions\n- Provider-issued deferral notices\n- Data source dependencies on managed resources being created\n\n**Handling:**\n- Marked as deferred in plan\n- Not executed during this apply\n- Requires subsequent plan/apply to complete\n- Stored in state for next run\n\n### 6.4 Ephemeral Resources\n\n**Purpose**: Temporary resources that don't persist in state\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- Data source-like but for specific use cases\n- Values only exist during operation\n- Not stored in state\n- Recreated each plan/apply\n\n**Lifecycle:**\n- Opened at start of operation\n- Used by dependent resources\n- Closed at operation completion\n\n### 6.5 Resource Importing\n\n**Purpose**: Bring existing infrastructure under Terraform management\n\n**Flow:**\n- User specifies resource address and import ID\n- `nodeResourceImport` fetches remote state\n- Provider's `ReadResource` populates state with remote values\n- Configuration must match or manual editing required\n- State written for use in subsequent plans\n\n## Conclusion\n\nTerraform's plan/apply pipeline is a sophisticated system balancing:\n\n- **Correctness**: DAGs ensure proper ordering\n- **Performance**: Parallel execution maximizes throughput\n- **Reliability**: State snapshots and atomic updates ensure consistency\n- **Extensibility**: Hooks and interfaces enable customization\n- **Safety**: Immutable plans enable review before execution\n\nUnderstanding these architectural components is essential for:\n- Extending Terraform with custom providers\n- Building tools that invoke Terraform programmatically\n- Debugging complex infrastructure changes\n- Contributing to Terraform core development\n- Optimizing Terraform for specific use cases\n",

{
  "content": "# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan and apply operations are orchestrated through a sophisticated dependency graph system that coordinates resource lifecycle management, provider interactions, and state synchronization. This document provides a detailed technical explanation of how these components interact to execute infrastructure changes.\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 Graph Architecture\n\nThe Terraform execution model is built around a **Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG)** that represents resources, data sources, modules, and their dependencies. This graph is the foundation of Terraform's execution model and enables:\n\n- **Concurrent execution** of independent nodes\n- **Dependency ordering** to ensure correct sequencing\n- **Partial execution** through targeted operations\n- **Resource expansion** for count/for_each resources\n\n### 1.2 Graph Builders\n\nTerraform provides specialized graph builders for different operation types:\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n- **Purpose**: Constructs the execution graph for planning operations\n- **Input**: Current configuration, prior state, root module variables\n- **Key Fields**:\n  - `Config`: The desired infrastructure configuration\n  - `State`: Current infrastructure state\n  - `RootVariableValues`: User-provided variable inputs\n  - `Targets`: Optional resource filtering for targeted operations\n  - `ForceReplace`: Resource instances that must be replaced\n  - `ExternalProviderConfigs`: Pre-initialized provider instances\n\n- **Operation**: Makes decisions primarily based on configuration (desired state) rather than the current state\n- **Output**: An execution graph ready for the plan walk\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n- **Purpose**: Constructs the execution graph for applying a previously-generated plan\n- **Input**: Configuration, change set (diff), current state, plan variables\n- **Key Difference**: Operates from the plan diff rather than configuration, ensuring only changes explicitly in the plan are applied\n- **Protection Mechanism**: Prevents unintended modifications to resources not in the diff\n\n#### BasicGraphBuilder\n- **Purpose**: Generic graph construction framework\n- **Mechanism**: Executes a series of graph transformations (steps) sequentially\n- **Validation**: Automatically validates the resulting DAG is acyclic and valid\n\n### 1.3 Graph Transformation Pipeline\n\nGraph transformers modify and augment the graph through multiple sequential transformation steps. The pipeline follows a **visitor pattern** where each transformer can add nodes, remove nodes, and create edges.\n\n#### Core Transformation Types:\n\n**Configuration Transformers:**\n- `TransformConfig`: Attaches configuration blocks to resource nodes\n- `TransformProvider`: Adds provider configuration nodes\n- `TransformModule`: Handles module expansion and nesting\n\n**Reference Resolution:**\n- `TransformReference`: Analyzes code expressions to discover dependencies\n  - Identifies references from one resource to another\n  - Analyzes references in provisioner blocks, lifecycle rules, and count/for_each expressions\n  - Creates edges based on discovered dependencies\n\n**State and Schema Attachment:**\n- `TransformAttachState`: Attaches current state snapshots to nodes\n- `TransformAttachSchema`: Binds provider schemas to resource nodes\n- `TransformAttachConfigProvider`: Associates provider configurations with resources\n\n**Dynamic Expansion:**\n- `TransformExpand`: Handles resource instance expansion\n- `TransformResourceCount`: Expands resources with `count` meta-argument\n- `TransformModuleExpansion`: Expands module instances\n\n**Lifecycle Management:**\n- `TransformDestroyEdge`: Adds destruction dependency edges\n- `TransformDestroyPlannedDestroyCBD`: Handles create-before-destroy lifecycle rules\n- `TransformTransitiveReduction`: Optimizes graph by removing redundant transitive edges\n\n**Deferred Actions:**\n- `TransformDeferred`: Marks actions that cannot be evaluated as deferred\n\n**Orphan Handling:**\n- `TransformOrphanResource`: Identifies and marks removed resources for deletion\n- `TransformOrphanOutput`: Handles outputs removed from configuration\n\n### 1.4 Graph Node Types and Interfaces\n\nNodes in the graph represent different infrastructure objects and their operations:\n\n#### Base Node Types:\n- **Resources**: `nodeExpandPlannableResource`, `nodeResourcePlanInstance`, `nodeResourceApplyInstance`\n- **Modules**: `nodeModuleExpand`, represents module instantiation\n- **Providers**: `nodeProviderConfig`, manages provider initialization\n- **Variables**: `nodeRootVariable`, `nodeModuleVariable`, `nodeVariableValidation`\n- **Outputs**: `nodeOutput`, computes and manages outputs\n- **Locals**: `nodeLocal`, evaluates local values\n\n#### Node Interface Contracts:\n\n**GraphNodeReferenceable**\n```go\ntype GraphNodeReferenceable interface {\n    ReferenceableAddrs() []addrs.Referenceable\n}\n```\nIndicates that a node can be referenced by other nodes in expressions.\n\n**GraphNodeReferencer**\n```go\ntype GraphNodeReferencer interface {\n    References() []*addrs.Reference\n}\n```\nProvides the list of resources/variables this node depends on by analyzing its expressions.\n\n**GraphNodeDynamicExpandable**\nIndicates the node expands into multiple sub-nodes (e.g., count expansion):\n- Expansion happens during graph traversal\n- Sub-nodes are created dynamically based on variable values\n- Critical for handling `count` and `for_each` meta-arguments\n\n**GraphNodeExecutable**\n```go\ntype GraphNodeExecutable interface {\n    Execute(EvalContext, walkOperation) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\nNodes implementing this interface contain the actual logic executed during graph walks.\n\n### 1.5 Dependency Discovery\n\nDependencies are discovered through multiple mechanisms:\n\n1. **Expression Analysis**: Terraform parses all HCL expressions to identify references\n   - Resource attribute references: `aws_instance.example.id`\n   - Data source references: `data.aws_ami.example.id`\n   - Variable references: `var.instance_type`\n   - Local value references: `local.common_tags`\n\n2. **Explicit Dependencies**: The `depends_on` meta-argument creates explicit dependency edges\n   - Used when implicit dependencies cannot be discovered\n   - Analyzed by `TransformReference` and `graphNodeDependsOn` interface\n\n3. **Provider Dependencies**: Implicit dependencies on provider configurations\n   - Every resource depends on its configured provider node\n   - Ensures providers are initialized before resource operations\n\n4. **Lifecycle Dependencies**: Special edges for create-before-destroy operations\n   - New resource must be created before old is destroyed\n   - Handled by `TransformDestroyEdge` and CBD transformers\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Plugin Architecture\n\nTerraform uses a **plugin-based architecture** for providers, communicating via **gRPC** with provider processes:\n\n#### Initialization Flow:\n1. **Plugin Loading**: Providers are loaded from disk or network based on lock file\n2. **Process Launch**: Each unique provider gets its own process\n3. **Handshake**: Terraform and provider negotiate protocol version\n4. **Schema Retrieval**: Terraform fetches resource types and data sources offered\n\n### 2.2 Provider Instance Management\n\n#### contextPlugins Structure:\nMaintains lifecycle of all provider instances across an operation:\n```\ncontextPlugins\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 factories: map[addrs.Provider]providers.Factory\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 instances: map[addrs.AbsProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 schemas: map[addrs.AbsProviderConfig]providers.ProviderSchema\n```\n\n#### Provider Lifecycle Phases:\n\n**1. Initialization (Plan/Apply Start)**\n- `EvalContext.InitProvider()` creates provider instance\n- Called once per provider configuration\n- Establishes gRPC connection to provider process\n- Panics if provider already initialized (prevents accidental duplicate initialization)\n\n**2. Configuration (Before Operations)**\n- `EvalContext.ConfigureProvider()` passes HCL configuration to provider\n- Configuration merged from:\n  - Explicit `provider` blocks\n  - User input via `provider_input()` function\n  - Environment variables\n- Returns diagnostics if configuration invalid\n\n**3. Operation**\n- Provider instance available via `EvalContext.Provider(addr)`\n- Returns `providers.Interface` implementing operations:\n  - `GetSchema()`: Retrieve resource/data source schemas\n  - `ValidateResourceConfig()`: Validate resource configuration\n  - `PlanResourceChange()`: Determine what will change\n  - `ApplyResourceChange()`: Execute the change\n  - `ReadDataSource()`: Fetch data source values\n  - Several other operations for refresh, import, etc.\n\n**4. Cleanup**\n- `EvalContext.CloseProvider()` closes provider connection\n- Called when provider no longer needed\n- Releases gRPC connection and cleans up resources\n\n### 2.3 Resource Operation Delegation\n\nResource operations are delegated through a standard flow:\n\n#### Plan Time (Provider Methods):\n1. **ReadResource**: Fetch current remote state for comparison\n2. **PlanResourceChange**: Provider determines what action is needed\n   - Inputs: prior state, proposed new config, config marks\n   - Outputs: planned new state, action (create/update/delete/no-op)\n   - Provider implements custom logic to detect drift\n\n#### Apply Time (Provider Methods):\n1. **ApplyResourceChange**: Execute the planned action\n   - Inputs: prior state, planned state\n   - Outputs: final state after operation\n   - Provider handles all cloud API interactions\n2. **ReadResource**: Verify final state was achieved\n\n### 2.4 Provider Configuration Resolution\n\nProvider configuration involves multiple layers of merging:\n\n**Configuration Sources (in precedence order):**\n1. **Explicit `provider` blocks**: Hardcoded in configuration\n2. **User input**: From `provider_input()` interactive prompts\n3. **Environment variables**: Provider-specific env var support\n4. **Defaults**: Provider applies default values\n\n**Multi-alias Providers:**\n- Single provider type can be configured multiple times with different aliases\n- Each configuration creates separate provider instance\n- Resources select provider via `provider = \"type.alias\"` argument\n\n### 2.5 Provider Schema Management\n\nProvider schemas are cached to avoid repeated round-trips:\n\n- **PreloadedProviderSchemas**: Optional optimization in `ContextOpts`\n  - Caller can pre-load schemas already fetched elsewhere\n  - Avoids redundant provider initialization\n  - Must be accurate or runtime behavior becomes erratic\n\n- **Schema Caching**: Schemas cached per provider configuration address\n  - Retrieved via `EvalContext.ProviderSchema(addr)`\n  - Used for configuration validation and type checking\n  - Critical for error messages and expression evaluation\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nTerraform maintains a hierarchical state representation:\n\n```\nState\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Version: int (schema version)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Serial: int (monotonically incrementing change counter)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Lineage: string (tracks state file identity across snapshots)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Modules: map[addrs.ModuleInstance]Module\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Module (per module instance)\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 Outputs: map[string]OutputValue\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 Resources: map[string]Resource\n\u2502       \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Resource\n\u2502       \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 Instances: map[addrs.InstanceKey]InstanceObject\n\u2502       \u2502           \u2514\u2500\u2500 InstanceObject (per resource instance)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 Status: (Ready, Tainted, Deposed)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 AttrsJSON: []byte (actual resource attributes)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 Private: []byte (provider-specific metadata)\n\u2502       \u2502               \u2514\u2500\u2500 Deposed: []DeposedInstanceObject (for CBD)\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 (nested modules)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 CheckResults: map[addrs.AbsResourceInstance]CheckState\n```\n\n**Key Concepts:**\n- **Status**: Indicates health of instance (Ready, Tainted, Deposed)\n- **AttrsJSON**: Resource attributes stored as JSON for schema-agnostic access\n- **Private**: Provider-specific data opaque to Terraform core\n- **Deposed**: Previous version kept during create-before-destroy operations\n- **CheckResults**: Results from resource checks (assertions)\n\n### 3.2 State Snapshots and Concurrency\n\nState access during graph walks is carefully managed:\n\n**Snapshot Mechanism:**\n- State is snapshotted at the beginning of walks\n- Nodes read from the snapshot, not live state\n- Prevents inconsistencies from concurrent updates\n- Final state computed at walk end and persisted\n\n**Synchronization:**\n- `states.SyncState` wrapper adds locking\n- Prevents concurrent modification of in-memory state\n- Serializes writes while allowing multiple readers\n\n**Concurrency Model:**\n- Multiple graph nodes execute in parallel\n- Each node reads snapshot, computes changes, queues writes\n- After all nodes complete, writes applied atomically\n- Results in consistent state even with parallel execution\n\n### 3.3 State Changes During Plan and Apply\n\n#### Plan Phase:\n1. **Refresh**: Fetch current remote values (if not skipped)\n   - Provider.ReadResource() called for each managed resource\n   - Current remote state becomes prior state for comparison\n2. **Plan**: Compare prior state with configuration\n   - Provider.PlanResourceChange() determines action needed\n   - Actions: Create, Read, Update, Delete, No-op, Replace\n3. **Plan File**: Actions serialized to plan file for apply phase\n   - Includes configuration, prior state, proposed changes\n   - Enables apply phase to reproduce plan consistently\n\n#### Apply Phase:\n1. **Validation**: Verify plan still applies to current state\n   - Checks for external changes since plan creation\n   - Detects conflicts that would invalidate the plan\n2. **Application**: Execute planned changes\n   - Provider.ApplyResourceChange() performs operations\n   - State updated with new values from provider\n3. **Persistence**: Final state written to state file\n   - Serial incremented\n   - Lineage preserved for tracking\n   - Stored in backend (local, remote, etc.)\n\n### 3.4 State Backends and Remote Storage\n\nState backends provide persistence mechanisms:\n\n**Backend Responsibilities:**\n- **State Lock**: Prevent concurrent modifications\n  - `StateLocker` interface provides distributed locks\n  - Critical for teams sharing infrastructure\n  - Ensures serial execution of operations\n- **Remote Persistence**: Store state durably\n  - S3, Terraform Cloud, Azure Storage, etc.\n  - Backup and version control built-in\n- **State Versioning**: Track state history\n  - Backend may keep historical versions\n  - Enables recovery from accidental changes\n\n**State Manager (`statemgr.State`):**\n- Wraps backend storage\n- Implements atomic read/write semantics\n- Handles lock acquisition before writes\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Hook System\n\n### 4.1 Overall Execution Pipeline\n\n#### Command Invocation \u2192 Plan/Apply Cycle:\n\n```\nUser Command (terraform plan/apply)\n    \u2193\nLoad Configuration\n    \u2193\nLoad Prior State\n    \u2193\nCreate Context\n    \u251c\u2500 Initialize Plugins\n    \u251c\u2500 Configure Providers\n    \u2514\u2500 Set up Evaluation Context\n    \u2193\nBuild Graph (Plan-specific or Apply-specific)\n    \u251c\u2500 Apply Transformations\n    \u251c\u2500 Discover Dependencies\n    \u251c\u2500 Expand Resources\n    \u2514\u2500 Validate DAG\n    \u2193\nWalk Graph (Concurrent Execution)\n    \u251c\u2500 Topological Ordering\n    \u251c\u2500 Node Evaluation\n    \u251c\u2500 Provider Operations\n    \u2514\u2500 State Updates\n    \u2193\nReturn Results\n    \u251c\u2500 Plan: Serialized change set\n    \u2514\u2500 Apply: Updated state\n```\n\n### 4.2 Graph Walking and Execution\n\n#### Walker Pattern\n\nThe **GraphWalker** interface orchestrates execution:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    EvalContext() EvalContext\n    enterScope(evalContextScope) EvalContext\n    exitScope(evalContextScope)\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Provides evaluation context to nodes\n- Manages scope entry/exit for module traversal\n- Executes individual nodes via `Execute()`\n- Aggregates diagnostics\n\n#### ContextGraphWalker Implementation:\n\nThe main implementation coordinating actual work:\n\n**EvalContext Provisioning:**\n- Creates evaluation context per node\n- Context provides access to:\n  - Current module path\n  - State, configuration, variables\n  - Provider instances\n  - Hook callbacks\n  - Expression evaluation\n\n**Node Execution:**\n1. Determines if node is executable (`GraphNodeExecutable`)\n2. Calls `Execute()` method with eval context\n3. Collects and aggregates diagnostics\n4. Propagates panics with context\n\n**Parallelism Control:**\n- `parallelSem`: Semaphore limiting concurrent executions\n- Default parallelism: 10 (configurable)\n- Limits CPU pressure and provider rate throttling\n- Each node acquisition blocks until semaphore permits\n\n#### DAG Walk Implementation\n\nThe `dag.Walk()` function implements parallel graph traversal:\n\n**Algorithm:**\n1. **Topological Sort**: Vertices with no dependencies ready first\n2. **Async Dispatch**: Ready vertices sent to worker goroutines\n3. **Dependency Tracking**: Maintains in-flight work count\n4. **Completion Notifications**: Workers signal completion\n5. **Deadlock Detection**: Identifies cycles and halts\n6. **Aggregation**: Collects all diagnostics\n\n**Key Properties:**\n- Fully asynchronous, maximizes parallelism\n- Respects dependency edges\n- Stops on first error (with graceful shutdown of in-flight nodes)\n- Provides panic safety through recovery handlers\n\n### 4.3 Hook System and Extension Points\n\nHooks provide extension points for observing and controlling execution:\n\n#### Hook Interface\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Plan/Apply lifecycle\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, action, priorState, plannedNewState) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, newState, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan comparison (diff)\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, priorState, proposedNewState) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, action, priorState, plannedNewState) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Refresh operations\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, priorState) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk DeposedKey, priorState, newState) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName, err) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName, line string)\n\n    // Import operations\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Action invocations (Terraform 1.10+)\n    StartAction(id HookActionIdentity) (HookAction, error)\n    ProgressAction(id HookActionIdentity, progress string) (HookAction, error)\n    CompleteAction(id HookActionIdentity, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // State updates\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Shutdown signal\n    Stopping()\n}\n```\n\n#### Hook Action Control\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue HookAction = iota  // Continue normal execution\n    HookActionHalt                         // Halt immediately, cancel operation\n)\n```\n\nHooks can:\n- **Observe**: Log operations, collect metrics\n- **Control**: Return errors to halt execution\n- **Modify**: Update context during execution (in some hooks)\n- **Respond**: React to state updates\n\n#### Hook Registration and Invocation\n\n1. **Registration**: Hooks passed in `ContextOpts` during Context creation\n2. **Storage**: Stored in Context along with stop hook\n3. **Invocation**: Called via `EvalContext.Hook()` during node execution\n4. **Ordering**: All hooks called for each event (in registration order)\n5. **Aggregation**: First error halts execution, other hooks not called\n\n#### Internal Hooks\n\n**stopHook**: Built-in hook detecting graceful shutdown signals\n- Monitors SIGINT, SIGTERM signals\n- Sets stop context causing nodes to abort\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n- **UI Callbacks**: Update progress bars and status displays\n- **Logging**: Detailed operation logging\n- **Metrics**: Collect performance data\n- **Policy**: Enforce constraints (e.g., prevent certain resources)\n- **Testing**: Mock provider responses\n\n### 4.4 Plan-Specific Execution\n\n**PlanGraphBuilder** creates graph specific to planning:\n\n1. **Refresh**: Fetch current state (unless skipped)\n2. **Config Comparison**: Compare current with desired\n3. **Plan Generation**: Provider determines actions\n4. **Deferral Support**: Mark unplannable resources as deferred\n\n**Node Types Used:**\n- `nodeExpandPlannableResource`: Expansion for resources\n- `nodeResourcePlanInstance`: Planning for each instance\n- `nodeProviderConfig`: Provider initialization\n- `nodeRootVariable`: Variable evaluation\n- `nodeOutput`: Output value computation\n\n**Outputs:**\n- `plans.Plan` containing:\n  - Computed changes per resource\n  - Prior state snapshot\n  - Configuration snapshot\n  - Root variable values\n  - Timestamp for audit trail\n\n### 4.5 Apply-Specific Execution\n\n**ApplyGraphBuilder** creates graph specific to applying:\n\n1. **Validation**: Verify plan is still applicable\n2. **Provisioning**: Run provisioners after resources created\n3. **Application**: Execute provider operations\n4. **State Persistence**: Write updated state\n\n**Node Types Used:**\n- `nodeExpandApplyableResource`: Resource expansion\n- `nodeResourceApplyInstance`: Applying each instance\n- `nodeProviderConfig`: Provider initialization\n- `nodeProvisioner`: Provisioning execution\n\n**Key Differences from Plan:**\n- Operates on plan diff, not full configuration\n- Provider apply operations modify infrastructure\n- State written durably after completion\n- Provisions executed post-creation (if configured)\n\n### 4.6 Dynamic Expansion (count/for_each)\n\nResource instances are expanded dynamically during graph traversal:\n\n**Expansion Nodes:**\n- `nodeExpandPlannableResource` (plan phase)\n- `nodeExpandApplyableResource` (apply phase)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n1. **Parent Node**: Represents resource as a whole\n2. **Expansion Decision**: Evaluates `count` or `for_each` expression\n3. **Sub-node Creation**: Generates instance-specific nodes\n4. **Dynamic Dependency**: Instance sub-nodes added to graph dynamically\n5. **Parallel Execution**: Instances can execute in parallel\n\n**Dependency Propagation:**\n- Dependencies on unexpanded resource apply to all instances\n- Dependencies on specific instances specified via splat expressions\n- Inter-instance dependencies via implicit references\n\n### 4.7 Error Handling and Propagation\n\n**Diagnostic Aggregation:**\n- Each node execution returns `tfdiags.Diagnostics`\n- Collected in graph walk, returned to caller\n- Includes errors, warnings, and informational messages\n\n**Error Severity Levels:**\n- **Error**: Fatal, prevents apply execution\n- **Warning**: Non-fatal, operation continues\n- **Info**: Informational, for user awareness\n\n**Panic Safety:**\n- Panic in node execution caught and logged\n- Graph walk continues with other nodes\n- Panic converted to diagnostic error\n- Prevents entire process from crashing\n\n**Graceful Shutdown:**\n- On error, graph walk signals remaining nodes\n- Nodes check stop context, abort cleanly\n- In-flight operations completed or cancelled\n- Resources in partial states logged for recovery\n\n## 5. Component Integration\n\n### 5.1 Context as Central Coordinator\n\nThe `Context` struct serves as the central coordinator:\n\n```go\ntype Context struct {\n    meta *ContextMeta              // Working directory metadata\n    plugins *contextPlugins        // Provider/provisioner factories\n    hooks []Hook                   // Extension points\n    parallelSem Semaphore         // Concurrency control\n    runContext context.Context     // Cancellation support\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Owns plugins and hooks\n- Controls parallelism\n- Manages operation lifecycle\n- Coordinates graph building and walking\n\n### 5.2 EvalContext as State and Service Provider\n\nThe `EvalContext` provides all services nodes need:\n\n- **State Access**: Current and proposed state values\n- **Configuration**: Module configurations and variable values\n- **Provider Access**: Initialize, configure, and use providers\n- **Hook Dispatch**: Call registered hooks\n- **Expression Evaluation**: Evaluate HCL expressions\n- **Module Path**: Current position in module hierarchy\n\nImplemented by `ContextGraphWalker` during execution.\n\n### 5.3 Graph as Execution Plan\n\nThe `Graph` struct represents the execution plan:\n\n- **Vertices**: Individual infrastructure objects and operations\n- **Edges**: Dependency relationships\n- **Validation**: Ensures DAG structure (no cycles)\n- **Walking**: Traversal with node execution\n\n### 5.4 Plan as Bridge Between Phases\n\nThe `plans.Plan` struct bridges planning and application:\n\n- **Captures**: What will change and why\n- **Immutable**: Prevents accidental change between phases\n- **Serializable**: Can be reviewed, stored, transmitted\n- **Reproducible**: Apply reproduces plan consistently\n\n## 6. Advanced Topics\n\n### 6.1 Targeted Operations\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- User specifies resources to target via `-target` flag\n- `Targets` list passed to graph builders\n- `TransformTargets` removes untargeted resources from graph\n- Warnings issued that plan is incomplete\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Rescue partial failures\n- Manage dependencies manually\n- Operations on single resources\n- **Warning**: Can cause inconsistencies if dependencies crossed\n\n### 6.2 Create-Before-Destroy (CBD)\n\n**Lifecycle Rule** for zero-downtime updates:\n\n1. **Detection**: Resource has `lifecycle { create_before_destroy = true }`\n2. **Graph Modification**: `TransformDestroyEdge` reorders dependencies\n3. **Execution**:\n   - New resource created first\n   - Old resource destroyed after new is ready\n   - Prevents service interruption\n\n### 6.3 Deferred Actions\n\n**Purpose**: Handle situations where operations cannot be planned yet\n\n**Triggers:**\n- Unknown values in `count` or `for_each` expressions\n- Provider-issued deferral notices\n- Data source dependencies on managed resources being created\n\n**Handling:**\n- Marked as deferred in plan\n- Not executed during this apply\n- Requires subsequent plan/apply to complete\n- Stored in state for next run\n\n### 6.4 Ephemeral Resources\n\n**Purpose**: Temporary resources that don't persist in state\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- Data source-like but for specific use cases\n- Values only exist during operation\n- Not stored in state\n- Recreated each plan/apply\n\n**Lifecycle:**\n- Opened at start of operation\n- Used by dependent resources\n- Closed at operation completion\n\n### 6.5 Resource Importing\n\n**Purpose**: Bring existing infrastructure under Terraform management\n\n**Flow:**\n- User specifies resource address and import ID\n- `nodeResourceImport` fetches remote state\n- Provider's `ReadResource` populates state with remote values\n- Configuration must match or manual editing required\n- State written for use in subsequent plans\n\n## Conclusion\n\nTerraform's plan/apply pipeline is a sophisticated system balancing:\n\n- **Correctness**: DAGs ensure proper ordering\n- **Performance**: Parallel execution maximizes throughput\n- **Reliability**: State snapshots and atomic updates ensure consistency\n- **Extensibility**: Hooks and interfaces enable customization\n- **Safety**: Immutable plans enable review before execution\n\nUnderstanding these architectural components is essential for:\n- Extending Terraform with custom providers\n- Building tools that invoke Terraform programmatically\n- Debugging complex infrastructure changes\n- Contributing to Terraform core development\n- Optimizing Terraform for specific use cases\n",

# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture

## Overview

Terraform's plan and apply operations are orchestrated through a sophisticated dependency graph system that coordinates resource lifecycle management, provider interactions, and state synchronization. This document provides a detailed technical explanation of how these components interact to execute infrastructure changes.

## 1. Graph Builder System

### 1.1 Graph Architecture

The Terraform execution model is built around a **Directed Acyclic Graph (DAG)** that represents resources, data sources, modules, and their dependencies. This graph is the foundation of Terraform's execution model and enables:

- **Concurrent execution** of independent nodes
- **Dependency ordering** to ensure correct sequencing
- **Partial execution** through targeted operations
- **Resource expansion** for count/for_each resources

### 1.2 Graph Builders

Terraform provides specialized graph builders for different operation types:

#### PlanGraphBuilder
- **Purpose**: Constructs the execution graph for planning operations
- **Input**: Current configuration, prior state, root module variables
- **Key Fields**:
  - `Config`: The desired infrastructure configuration
  - `State`: Current infrastructure state
  - `RootVariableValues`: User-provided variable inputs
  - `Targets`: Optional resource filtering for targeted operations
  - `ForceReplace`: Resource instances that must be replaced
  - `ExternalProviderConfigs`: Pre-initialized provider instances

- **Operation**: Makes decisions primarily based on configuration (desired state) rather than the current state
- **Output**: An execution graph ready for the plan walk

#### ApplyGraphBuilder
- **Purpose**: Constructs the execution graph for applying a previously-generated plan
- **Input
... (truncated)
